# CODEX RECOVERY AND INTEGRATION PROMPT

## User
**Timestamp:** 2026-07-19T00:10:14.081Z

CODEX RECOVERY AND INTEGRATION PROMPT

Consolidate Vision Waypoint Phases B-1 Through B-6 Into One Canonical Application

You are performing a complete recovery, audit, reconciliation, and integration of the Vision Waypoint Phase B implementation.

The implementation appears to have been developed across multiple separate Git worktrees or cloned working directories:

Codex_TreasureHunt
Codex_TreasureHunt-phaseb2
Codex_TreasureHunt-phaseb3
Codex_TreasureHunt-phaseb4
Codex_TreasureHunt-phaseb5
Codex_TreasureHunt-phaseb6

These phase directories were intended to support parallel work, not to become permanently separate applications.

The final required result is:

One canonical repository
One integrated codebase
One coherent database migration history
One shared set of domain contracts
One shared Player interface
One shared Captain interface
One shared Studio interface
One canonical development server
One canonical port: 3000

Do not blindly copy files from one phase directory into another.

Do not assume that a Codex chat reporting completion means its work was merged.

Do not assume GitHub main contains all completed Phase B work.

Do not delete any worktree, clone, folder, branch, commit, migration, untracked file, or local change until the complete recovery and integration has been reviewed.

⸻

1. Primary Mission

Recover and integrate all legitimate work from Vision Waypoint Phases B-1 through B-6 into one canonical integration branch.

You must:

1. Identify the exact repository/worktree arrangement.
2. Preserve every phase implementation.
3. Determine what each phase actually completed.
4. Identify all branches, commits, uncommitted changes, and generated artifacts.
5. Compare each phase against its original governing prompt.
6. Reconcile overlapping source changes.
7. Consolidate database migrations.
8. Consolidate domain and protocol contracts.
9. Port phase functionality into the current canonical UI.
10. Run focused validation after each phase is integrated.
11. Run complete validation after all phases are combined.
12. Publish the integration branch safely.
13. Produce a detailed integration and recovery report.
14. Stop for review before merging into main.
15. Preserve all phase worktrees until final approval.

This is both:

* a repository recovery task;
* and a full software integration task.

It is not merely a Git merge exercise.

⸻

2. Governing Source-of-Truth Order

Before modifying source, locate and read all applicable governing material.

The governing order is:

1. TT-VISION-GOV-001
   Vision Waypoint and External AR Governing Specification
2. TT-VISION-PHASE-B-001
   Phase B Implementation Roadmap
3. Original prompts for Phases B-1 through B-6
4. Phase-specific ADRs and implementation records
5. Existing project-wide architecture and design documentation
6. Current canonical repository conventions
7. This recovery and integration prompt

Expected locations may include:

Development_Docs/
Development_Docs/AR/
Development_Docs/AR/ADRs/
Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B1/
Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B2/
Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B3/
Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B4/
Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B5/
Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B6/
Codex_Chats/

Search thoroughly.

Do not invent replacement architecture merely because phase implementations disagree.

When two implementations conflict, use the governing documents and semantic dependency order to determine the correct combined design.

Record any material decision in an ADR or integration decision log.

⸻

3. Non-Negotiable Safety Rules

Before changing anything:

1. Identify the canonical repository path.
2. Identify every Codex_TreasureHunt-phaseb* directory.
3. Determine whether each directory is:
    * a linked Git worktree;
    * a separate full clone;
    * a copied folder;
    * a detached worktree;
    * a generated build output;
    * or another arrangement.
4. Record the exact state of every directory.
5. Preserve all staged changes.
6. Preserve all unstaged changes.
7. Preserve all untracked files.
8. Preserve all local branches.
9. Preserve all stashes.
10. Preserve all phase-specific commits.
11. Preserve all migration files.
12. Preserve all phase documentation and completion reports.

Never use:

git reset --hard
git clean
git checkout -- .
git restore .
git restore --staged .
git stash --all
force push
broad file-copy replacement
automatic conflict resolution using only ours
automatic conflict resolution using only theirs

Do not delete or remove any worktree.

Do not run cleanup tools against the phase folders.

Do not allow generated dependency folders such as node_modules, .next, build output, caches, or temporary databases to influence source integration.

Do not stage unrelated files using broad commands such as:

git add .
git add -A

Stage intentionally by path.

⸻

4. Canonical Recovery Branch

Perform the recovery from the canonical Codex_TreasureHunt repository.

Create a dedicated integration branch, for example:

integration/vision-waypoint-b1-b6

The integration branch must be based on the correct current canonical branch.

Before creating it, record:

* canonical branch;
* canonical HEAD;
* upstream;
* ahead/behind status;
* remote HEAD;
* worktree status;
* untracked files;
* active development server;
* current database configuration;
* current port usage.

Do not modify main directly.

Do not merge the integration branch into main automatically.

Push the integration branch after successful checkpoints and final validation.

⸻

5. Complete Worktree and Clone Inventory

From the canonical repository, run and record:

git worktree list --porcelain
git branch --all --verbose
git log --all --graph --decorate --oneline
git remote -v
git status --short --branch
git stash list

Inside every Phase B directory, run:

git rev-parse --show-toplevel
git rev-parse --git-common-dir
git rev-parse --git-dir
git branch --show-current
git rev-parse HEAD
git rev-parse --abbrev-ref --symbolic-full-name @{upstream}
git status --short --branch
git remote -v
git stash list
git log --oneline --decorate --max-count=30
git merge-base HEAD main

If an upstream does not exist, record that fact without treating it as failure.

For every directory, record:

Absolute path
Repository identity
Worktree or clone
Branch
HEAD commit
Base commit
Remote
Upstream
Ahead/behind state
Staged files
Unstaged files
Untracked files
Stashes
Relevant commits
Build artifacts
Database files
Environment files
Last modified time

Create:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B_Worktree_Inventory.md

⸻

6. Preserve Uncommitted Phase Work

If any phase folder contains uncommitted source changes:

1. Inspect every changed file.
2. Separate source from generated output.
3. Do not commit:
    * node_modules;
    * .next;
    * build output;
    * logs;
    * temporary database copies;
    * local secrets;
    * caches.
4. Create a preservation branch specific to that phase if needed.
5. Commit legitimate uncommitted source with a clearly labeled recovery commit.

Example:

recovery/phase-b4-uncommitted

Example commit:

recovery(vision): preserve uncommitted phase B-4 work

Do not alter the intent of the work during preservation.

The initial goal is to ensure that no source exists only as an uncommitted local file.

⸻

7. Recover Separate Clone History

If any phase directory is a separate clone rather than a shared worktree:

1. Verify that it points to the same repository origin.
2. Identify its unique branch and commits.
3. Add it temporarily as a local recovery remote if necessary.
4. Fetch the relevant branch and commit history into the canonical repository.
5. Preserve exact commit identities where practical.
6. Do not push unrelated local branches.
7. Do not overwrite an existing branch with a different history.

Example temporary remote names:

phaseb2-recovery
phaseb3-recovery
phaseb4-recovery
phaseb5-recovery
phaseb6-recovery

After fetching, verify that every unique source commit can be addressed from the canonical repository.

Document the recovery method.

⸻

8. Phase Provenance and Completeness Audit

Create a full provenance matrix for B-1 through B-6.

For each phase, identify:

* original prompt;
* governing requirements;
* source folder;
* source branch;
* starting commit;
* ending commit;
* merge base;
* unique commit range;
* changed source files;
* deleted files;
* migration files;
* schema changes;
* dependencies added;
* environment variables added;
* API routes added;
* domain types added;
* protocol types added;
* frontend components added;
* native/desktop files added;
* PWA files added;
* tests added;
* documentation added;
* implementation record;
* completion report;
* test results claimed;
* test results reproducible;
* uncommitted work;
* pushed state;
* merged state;
* conflicts with other phases;
* stale-base risks;
* placeholder or mock status;
* actual completion percentage.

Create:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B1_B6_Provenance_Matrix.md
  Phase_B1_B6_Changed_Files.csv
  Phase_B1_B6_Test_Evidence.md
  Phase_B1_B6_Completion_Assessment.md

Do not classify a phase as complete based only on:

* chat completion;
* documentation;
* scaffolding;
* placeholder interfaces;
* a passing typecheck;
* mock-only behavior where production behavior was required;
* isolated build success.

Use source and test evidence.

⸻

9. Dependency Analysis

Determine the actual logical dependencies among B-1 through B-6.

The default expectation is:

B-1
Shared platform, domain, versioning, protocol, adapters
B-2
Capture companion and acquisition infrastructure
B-3
Vision build, package, inference, and verification pipeline
B-4
Studio authoring, reference collection, calibration, testing
B-5
Player and Captain runtime integration
B-6
Production hardening, rollout, observability, certification

Do not assume all phases were implemented from the output of the prior phase.

Check each phase’s merge base.

If B-3, B-4, B-5, or B-6 were all created directly from B-1, integration must explicitly combine their independent changes.

Create:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B_Dependency_Graph.md

Identify:

* hard dependencies;
* soft dependencies;
* overlapping files;
* overlapping migrations;
* overlapping contracts;
* ordering constraints;
* required adaptation work.

⸻

10. Integration Plan Before Code Changes

Before merging or cherry-picking any implementation commit, create:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B1_B6_Integration_Plan.md

The plan must define:

1. Integration order.
2. Branches or commit ranges to incorporate.
3. Commits to exclude.
4. Reasons for exclusions.
5. Shared files likely to conflict.
6. Database migration strategy.
7. Contract consolidation strategy.
8. UI adaptation strategy.
9. Test sequence.
10. Rollback checkpoints.
11. Validation ownership.
12. Port and server isolation.
13. Database isolation.
14. Final publication plan.

Do not begin broad integration until this plan exists.

⸻

11. Commit Selection Rules

For each phase, classify commits into:

APPLICATION_SOURCE
DATABASE_MIGRATION
TESTS
DOCUMENTATION
CHAT_SYNC
GENERATED_OUTPUT
ENVIRONMENT_ONLY
RECOVERY
UNRELATED

Integrate:

* application source;
* legitimate migrations;
* tests;
* relevant documentation;
* relevant recovery commits.

Usually exclude or separately handle:

* chat synchronization commits;
* generated build artifacts;
* local environment files;
* dependency caches;
* unrelated product work;
* duplicate documentation synchronization.

Do not cherry-pick chat-sync commits merely because they are adjacent to application commits.

Do not lose phase implementation work hidden inside mixed commits. If a mixed commit contains both application source and unrelated changes, extract the relevant patch carefully and document it.

⸻

12. Controlled Phase Integration

Integrate each phase in the dependency order determined by the roadmap and audit.

The expected checkpoint sequence is:

integration(vision): incorporate phase B-1 foundation
integration(vision): incorporate phase B-2 capture infrastructure
integration(vision): incorporate phase B-3 vision pipeline
integration(vision): incorporate phase B-4 studio tooling
integration(vision): incorporate phase B-5 runtime experience
integration(vision): incorporate phase B-6 hardening

After each phase:

1. Resolve conflicts semantically.
2. Run formatting on changed files.
3. Run focused typecheck.
4. Run focused unit tests.
5. Run focused schema tests.
6. Run focused integration tests.
7. Record failures and fixes.
8. Create a checkpoint commit.
9. Push the integration branch.
10. Continue only when the current checkpoint is coherent.

Do not wait until all phases are merged before discovering that B-2 broke B-1’s contracts.

⸻

13. Conflict Resolution Rules

Never resolve a conflict using blanket “ours” or “theirs.”

For each conflict:

1. Identify which phase introduced each side.
2. Identify the governing requirement.
3. Identify newer canonical improvements on main.
4. Determine whether both sides contain valid behavior.
5. Build the combined implementation.
6. Add or update tests proving the resolution.
7. Record the decision.

Maintain:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B_Conflict_Resolution_Log.md

For every conflict record:

File
Phases involved
Original intent
Conflict cause
Chosen behavior
Code retained from each side
Tests added
Remaining limitation

⸻

14. Protect Current Canonical UI Work

The current canonical branch may contain newer:

* navigation;
* unified shell;
* color system;
* responsive behavior;
* Tall Tale journal UI;
* accessibility improvements;
* animation changes;
* Player Library changes;
* Captain Library changes;
* Studio changes.

Do not restore stale phase-specific UI wholesale.

Where a phase branch contains functionality but older presentation code:

1. Extract the functional behavior.
2. Port it into the current canonical component structure.
3. Use the current design system.
4. Preserve current navigation.
5. Preserve current color/theme behavior.
6. Preserve current responsive layout.
7. Preserve current accessibility behavior.
8. Preserve canonical journal usage.

The final product must not feel like six different applications taped together at the edges.

⸻

15. Shared Contract Consolidation

Create one authoritative implementation for each shared contract.

Explicitly audit and reconcile:

* VisionWaypoint;
* VisionWaypointVersion;
* lifecycle states;
* verification profiles;
* sharing scopes;
* publication metadata;
* story waypoint binding;
* capture request;

* package schema version;
* runtime compatibility;

* verification result;
* confidence and evidence;
* Captain decision;
* progression event;
* feature flags;
* capability detection;
* platform adapters;
* desktop bridge;
* PWA bridge;
* protocol errors;
* telemetry;
* audit records.

There must not be phase-local duplicate versions of these contracts after integration.

Use schema validation at trust boundaries.

Preserve backwards compatibility where required.

Document any schema version bump.

⸻

16. Database and Migration Reconciliation

Database integration must remain serialized.

Create:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B_Migration_Ledger.md

For every migration record:

* phase;
* filename;
* parent schema state;
* models added;
* fields added;
* fields changed;
* indexes;
* unique constraints;
* foreign keys;
* data migrations;
* rollback implications;
* whether it was applied anywhere;
* conflict with another phase.

Identify whether phases created migrations independently from the same schema baseline.

Do not simply sort conflicting migrations by timestamp.

The final migration history must support:

1. Clean database bootstrap.
2. Upgrade from the canonical pre-B schema.
3. Upgrade from B-1-only schema.
4. Seeded development database.
5. Test database creation.
6. ORM client generation.
7. Rollback or recovery documentation.

Preserve published-version immutability.

Preserve idempotency constraints.

Preserve exact-once story progression.

Preserve referential integrity.

If necessary, create a new integration migration that reconciles independent phase changes.

Do not edit already-applied production migrations unless absolutely necessary and documented.

⸻

17. Exactly-Once and Concurrency Verification

The combined system must prove:

* repeated verification submissions do not create duplicate accepted events;
* repeated processing does not advance the story twice;
* reused idempotency keys with altered payloads are rejected;
* stale verification results cannot advance a later story block;
* Captain fallback cannot double-complete an objective;
* automatic verification and Captain confirmation cannot both advance the story;
* retries are distinguishable from duplicates;
* session concurrency is enforced;
* publication cannot mutate an existing published waypoint version.

Use database transactions for multi-step state changes.

Unique constraints alone are not sufficient proof.

⸻

18. Front-End Integration Requirements

The final integrated application must use one shared frontend.

Studio

Integrate:

* waypoint library;
* create waypoint;
* edit draft;
* version history;
* reference collection;
* build status;
* calibration;
* test workflow;
* publication;
* immutable-version display;
* story binding;
* compatibility status;
* error recovery.

Player

Integrate:

* waypoint objective;
* Inspect Surroundings;
* permission state;
* capture state;
* verification progress;
* matched;
* not matched;
* low confidence;
* retry;
* timeout;
* offline;
* unavailable capability;
* Captain fallback;
* accessible status announcements;
* deterministic final story state.

Captain

Integrate:

* active verification requests;
* attempt history;
* safe evidence summary;
* accept;
* reject;
* request retry;
* fallback resolution;
* audit history;
* stale-request behavior.

Shared

Preserve:

* canonical navigation;
* current design system;
* current theme;
* responsive behavior;
* accessibility;
* motion preferences;
* role boundaries;
* Player-safe data projection.

⸻

19. Desktop and PWA Consolidation

The final system must not contain separate duplicated applications for:

* browser;
* PWA;
* Windows desktop.

The shared frontend must remain canonical.

Platform differences must exist behind adapters.

Audit:

* PWA manifest;
* service worker;
* cache boundaries;
* offline behavior;
* desktop shell;
* desktop bridge;
* capability detection;
* capture adapter;
* filesystem adapter;
* update behavior;
* protocol pairing;
* local service communication.

Do not cache private mutable API responses.

Do not store secrets in desktop source.

Do not permit silent capture.

Do not create a second desktop-only story engine.

⸻

20. Feature Flag Consolidation

Create one authoritative feature-flag system.

At minimum reconcile:

visionWaypoints.enabled
visionWaypoints.studio.enabled
visionWaypoints.player.enabled
visionWaypoints.mockVerifier.enabled
visionWaypoints.capture.enabled
visionWaypoints.buildPipeline.enabled
visionWaypoints.externalProvider.enabled
visionWaypoints.captainFallback.enabled
visionWaypoints.pwa.enabled
visionWaypoints.desktop.enabled

Feature flags and runtime capabilities must remain separate.

The UI must resolve:

feature enabled
platform supported
permission available
provider available
package compatible
offline capable
fallback available

Do not expose controls that cannot function.

⸻

21. Security and Privacy Review

Perform a focused security review covering:

* raw frame handling;
* screenshot handling;
* evidence retention;
* pairing tokens;
* provider authentication;
* request replay;
* session binding;
* waypoint-version binding;
* package hash validation;
* unsupported schema versions;
* unsafe external input;
* API authorization;
* Captain permissions;
* Studio publication permissions;
* local desktop bridge exposure;
* service-worker caching;
* logging of private story data.

Do not store raw image data in generic JSON fields.

Do not expose unpublished waypoint data to Players.

Do not allow a provider result to claim Captain authority.

Do not silently capture frames.

Record findings in:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B_Security_Privacy_Review.md

⸻

22. Test and Validation Environment Isolation

Before mutating tests:

1. Identify the canonical database.
2. Create a unique isolated test database or copy.
3. Use an explicit absolute database connection.
4. Record the database identity.
5. Record the development server PID.
6. Record the validation port.
7. Verify the application is connected to the isolated database.
8. Preserve the canonical database hash, size, and modification time.
9. Run mutations only against the isolated test database.
10. Verify the canonical database remains unchanged.

Do not run integration tests against a shared local development database.

Do not use port 3000 for temporary validation if the existing canonical server already owns it.

Temporary isolated ports are allowed during integration.

The final canonical application must run on port 3000.

⸻

23. Required Focused Tests

After integrating each phase, run the relevant focused tests.

The final integrated suite must include:

Domain

* waypoint creation;
* draft version creation;
* immutable publication;
* new draft from published version;
* lifecycle transition validation;
* compatibility validation;
* story binding to exact version.

Protocol

* valid request;
* invalid schema;
* unsupported schema;
* wrong waypoint version;
* wrong package hash;
* wrong session;
* expired request;
* duplicate event;
* altered duplicate payload;
* invalid confidence;
* invalid provider authority.

Story engine

* successful verification completes once;
* failed verification does not complete;
* retry succeeds;
* duplicate success does not duplicate progression;
* stale success does not progress;
* Captain confirmation completes once;
* automatic and Captain paths cannot both complete;
* refresh does not repeat completion.

Studio

* create;
* edit;
* publish;
* clone version;
* bind;
* preview;
* calibration failure;
* incompatible package;
* validation errors.

Player

* ready;
* requesting;
* capturing;
* verifying;
* success;
* failure;
* retry;
* timeout;
* offline;
* unsupported;
* Captain fallback;
* keyboard;
* screen reader;
* reduced motion.

Captain

* request list;
* detail;
* approve;
* reject;
* retry request;
* stale request;
* duplicate decision;
* audit history.

PWA and desktop

* capability resolution;
* adapter selection;
* unsupported fallback;
* offline shell;
* safe caching;
* desktop bridge validation;
* no duplicate frontend implementation.

⸻

24. Required End-to-End Proof

Run a complete isolated end-to-end workflow:

Studio creates waypoint
        ↓
Draft version is persisted
        ↓
Reference data is attached or mocked as allowed
        ↓
Build/test process runs
        ↓
Immutable version is published
        ↓
Story block binds exact published version
        ↓
Story is published
        ↓
Playthrough starts
        ↓
Player reaches waypoint objective
        ↓
Inspect Surroundings is invoked
        ↓
Correct platform adapter runs
        ↓
Verification request is persisted
        ↓
Verification result is validated
        ↓
Story advances exactly once
        ↓
Browser refresh occurs
        ↓
Story remains advanced once
        ↓
Duplicate result is submitted
        ↓
No duplicate progression occurs

Also prove:

Failure
Retry
Timeout
Stale result
Captain confirmation
Unsupported capability
Offline behavior
Package incompatibility

Record exact requests, events, database rows, and terminal states without exposing secrets.

⸻

25. Runtime and Port Consolidation

At the end of integration:

* one canonical source tree must contain all Phase B functionality;
* one canonical development command must start the app;
* one canonical environment must be documented;
* one canonical database configuration must be used;
* one canonical development server must run on port 3000.

Do not leave phase-specific builds presented as separate product versions.

Phase worktrees may remain for safety, but they must not be required to run the application.

Document which old ports were used temporarily and confirm they are not part of the final workflow.

⸻

26. Final Repository Validation

Run repository-supported commands, including appropriate equivalents of:

npm run format:check
npm run lint
npm run typecheck
npm test
npm run assets:validate
npm run build
npm run validate

Also run:

* database migration validation;
* clean bootstrap;
* seeded bootstrap;
* protocol compatibility tests;
* focused Phase B E2E;
* PWA build validation;
* desktop build validation where supported.

Do not run multiple full validation suites concurrently against the same build directory or database.

Classify every result as:

PASS
FAIL
SKIPPED
BLOCKED
ENVIRONMENTAL
BASELINE FAILURE
TASK REGRESSION

A skipped test is not a pass.

⸻

Create:

For each B-1 through B-6:

* original requirements;

* commands;

Final state

* canonical application path;
* canonical start command;
* canonical server port;
* integration branch URL;
* draft PR if created;
* worktrees preserved;
* recommendation for eventual worktree removal.

⸻

28. GitHub Publication

Push the integration branch to GitHub.

Open a draft pull request targeting main.

The draft PR must include:

* phase provenance summary;
* integration sequence;
* migration notes;
* conflict summary;
* validation summary;
* known limitations;
* worktrees preserved;
* explicit statement that the PR is not yet merged.

Do not merge the PR automatically.

Do not delete source branches automatically.

Do not remove worktrees automatically.

Stop for human review after the integration branch and report are complete.

⸻

29. Completion Gate

Do not declare this task complete unless all of the following are true:

1. Every phase directory has been inventoried.
2. Every phase branch and commit is accounted for.
3. Every uncommitted source change has been preserved.
4. Every phase has been assessed against its original prompt.
5. All valid Phase B source exists in one integration branch.
6. No entire phase folder was copied blindly over another.
7. Shared contracts have one authoritative implementation.
8. Database migrations form one valid sequence.
9. Published waypoint versions remain immutable.
10. Story progression remains exactly-once.
11. Stale results cannot progress the story.
12. Player, Captain, and Studio use one shared application.
13. Browser, PWA, and desktop use shared frontend source.
14. The current canonical UI and navigation are preserved.
15. Focused tests pass or failures are documented.
16. Full validation passes or blockers are documented.
17. The integrated application runs from the canonical repository.
18. The canonical application runs on port 3000.
19. The integration branch is pushed.
20. A draft PR is created.
21. The final report is complete.
22. Old phase folders and worktrees remain preserved.
23. Nothing has been merged to main without review.

Recover the work, integrate it carefully, validate it thoroughly, publish the integration branch, create the draft PR, and stop for review.

## Tool Call: exec
**Timestamp:** 2026-07-19T00:11:35.533Z

const ids = [
  "019f771a-30e8-7cc2-9dfd-87180f1919e6",
  "019f7728-8944-7cb3-85aa-90e273fc7cd6"
];
for (const id of ids) {
  const r = await tools.codex_app__read_thread({threadId:id, turnLimit:1, includeOutputs:false});
  const obj = typeof r === "string" ? JSON.parse(r) : r;
  const turn = obj.turns?.[0];
  const messages = (turn?.items || []).filter(x => x.type === "agentMessage" || x.type === "userMessage").slice(-8).map(x => ({
    type:x.type,
    phase:x.phase,
    text:(x.text || x.content?.map(c=>c.text).filter(Boolean).join(" ") || "").slice(0,1200).replace(/\s+/g," ")
  }));
  text(JSON.stringify({id,status:obj.thread?.status,startedAt:turn?.startedAt,turnStatus:turn?.status,messages}, null, 2));
}

unsigned installer hash recorded\n\nThis was not independently rerun during this audit.\n\n### Contradictions and material gaps\n\n1. **Exact-once proof is incomplete.**\n\n   The duplicate E2E replays the same idempotency key internally and proves one `verificationSatisfied` event. It does not test distinct-key or concurrent submissions against the same request, altered-payload reuse of an existing idempotency key, or automatic/Captain races. `submitVerification` checks request status before its transaction and does not recheck it transactionally; multiple distinct accepted events remain possible even though `completeBlock` suppresses a second block completion.\n\n2. **Database immutability/reference constraints are incomplete.**\n\n   Services prevent published edits and reject draft bindings, but the database does not constrain `StoryWaypointBinding.waypointVersionId` to a published version, does not ensure `waypointId` matches the referenced version’s waypoint, and has no published-row update trigger. The roadmap explicitly asked migration constraints to prevent published stories referencing editable drafts.\n\n3. **Publication is not idempotent.**\n\n   Repeating `publishDraftVersion` throws `PUBLISHED_VERSION_IMMUTABLE`; the roadmap requires build/publication operations to be idempotent.\n\n4. **Two incompatible `VisionCapabilities` contracts exist.**\n\n   `src/vision/protocol.ts` defines governed capabilities such as `nativeCapture`, `globalHotkeys`, and `localInference`; `src/vision/platform-adapters.ts` independently defines a different `VisionCapabilities` shape using `capture`, `deterministicMock`, and `platform`. This violates the single-authoritative-contract goal.\n\n5. **Feature flags are mostly declarative.**\n\n   Only selected APIs/progression use flags. `publicVisionFeatureFlags` is unused; Studio always shows the Vision link, PWA registration is always mounted, adapter selection ignores flags/capabilities, and most future flags appear only in resolution/diagnostics. The requirement that disabled functionality be hidden and nonfunctional is not met.\n\n6. **Captain interface is partial.**\n\n   The Captain component is read-only diagnostics plus copy-summary. It lacks the required UI actions for scenario selection, start, cancel, duplicate replay, stale simulation, approve, reject, and retry. An untested approve/reject API exists; no retry action exists. The completion report’s “approve/reject/retry fallbacks” claim is unsupported.\n\n7. **Player cancellation is partial.**\n\n   Releasing early cancels only the local pre-attempt hold timer. Once the request starts there is no visible in-flight Cancel control, although a cancel API/adapter method exists.\n\n8. **Desktop parity evidence is weaker than claimed.**\n\n   The packaged smoke verifies the local shared page title. The E2E “desktop path” posts `platform: DESKTOP` directly to HTTP; it does not instantiate `DesktopPlatformAdapter`, invoke the real preload bridge from the renderer, or navigate Player/Captain/Studio in the packaged shell.\n\n9. **PWA installability is not fully proven.**\n\n   Tests inspect manifest/service-worker/offline policy, but no browser installability audit or actual install/launch flow was recorded. The completion report acknowledges no OS-level install ceremony.\n\n10. **Test coverage is broad but not as comprehensive as the prompt.**\n\n   Source-specific tests comprise 3 domain cases, 2 protocol cases, 2 adapter cases, 1 permission case, 2 flag cases, 2 PWA policy cases, 2 Electron cases, and 2 large E2E cases. Missing focused coverage includes lifecycle services, live MySQL, migration downgrade/reference constraints, disabled UI behavior, actual Desktop adapter parity, Captain actions, in-flight cancel, and concurrency/altered-duplicate behavior.\n\n11. **Completion report format is noncompliant.**\n\n   It never states the required `PASS`, `PASS WITH DOCUMENTED LIMITATIONS`, or `FAIL`, while claiming implementation completion despite unchecked B1 obligations. The B-3 E2E locks the same target-reference recording used for authoring. Thus locked evidence is reused as reference/tuning input, contrary to the governing no-leakage rule.\n\n   Evidence:\n\n   - `src/vision/authoring.ts:646-713`\n   - `tests/e2e/vision-waypoint-b3.spec.ts:136,196-217`\n\n2. **BuildInput is not independently schema-validated**\n\n   There is no runtime Zod BuildInput schema or parse. The service constructs, sorts, serializes, and hashes a plain object. The OpenAPI contract leaves most nested objects untyped.\n\n   `buildInputFor()` also omits governed configuration already held by the draft, including creator-guidance preferences, Captain fallback, story-purpose configuration, and full capture/transformation/cloud-state data.\n\n3. **Readiness permits materially insufficient evidence**\n\n   Data Health can pass with one target recording, one target region, one generic boundary, and only nearby/distant negatives. It does not enforce:\n\n   - required strict/story-critical boundary categories;\n   - invalid viewpoint evidence;\n   - correct-island/wrong-landmark evidence;\n   - target coverage by angle/distance;\n   - multi-view important regions;\n   - environmental evidence;\n   - contradictory region/distance checks;\n   - capability/schema/cloud compatibility.\n\n4. **Unsaved-edit loss paths**\n\n   Conflict handling immediately calls `load()` and replaces local form state. Autosave responses also replace the form and clear `dirty`, so edits typed while a save is in flight can be overwritten.\n\n   Evidence: `VisionWaypointEditor.tsx:431-458`.\n\n5. **Destructive media deletion order**\n\n   The UI deletes the local Companion artifact before server authorization/tombstoning. Network, CSRF, or concurrent-reference failure can leave the database pointing at missing local media.\n\n   Evidence: `RecordingReview.tsx:63` followed by the server DELETE request.\n\n6. **Cloud consent is not enforced**\n\n   `CLOUD_ASSISTED` with `rawMediaConsent: false` validates and is not health-blocked. Local-only assets are not prevented from cloud build preparation.\n\n7. **Published-version metadata can change through a draft**\n\n   Saving Purpose mutates shared `VisionWaypoint.type`, while published versions reference the same waypoint identity. MySQL `0009` correctly creates them.\n\n   Clean bootstrap can pass while still having this drift because `migrate deploy` does not compare the resulting physical schema with declared Prisma relations.\n\n2. **The MySQL command sequence skips B6.**\n\n   Unified [package.json](C:\\Users\\kkids\\Documents\\Codex_TreasureHunt_Consolidation\\package.json) exposes scripts for `0005` through `0009`, then jumps to `0011`. required minimum error codes.\n- Deterministic scenarios cover verified, insufficient, not-at-target, ambiguous, system error, delayed, cancelled, stale, and duplicate delivery.\n- Shared Next.js UI is packaged by Electron and exposed as a PWA; there is no duplicated frontend tree.\n- Service-worker policy is static-shell only and network-only for APIs/authenticated surfaces.\n- Electron bridge is narrow: `vision.getCapabilities`, `vision.prepareMockScan`, and `app.getDiagnostics`.\n\nHistorical transcript evidence shows:\n\n- Full validation exit `0`\n- 33 Vitest files / 102 tests passed\n- 2 Electron bridge tests passed\n- 24 Playwright passed / 8 WebKit mutation tests skipped\n- clean six-migration SQLite bootstrap\n- production build/restart passed\n- desktop build/smoke passed\n- unsigned installer hash recorded\n\nThis was not independently rerun during this audit.\n\n### Contradictions and material gaps\n\n1. **Exact-once proof is incomplete.**\n\n   The duplicate E2E replays the same idempotency key internally and proves one `verificationSatisfied` event. It does not test distinct-key or concurrent submissions against the same request, altered-payload reuse of an existing idempotency key, or automatic/Captain races. `submitVerification` checks request status before its transaction and does not recheck it transactionally; multiple distinct accepted events remain possible even though `completeBlock` suppresses a second block completion.\n\n2. **Database immutability/reference constraints are incomplete.**\n\n   Services prevent published edits and reject draft bindings, but the database does not constrain `StoryWaypointBinding.waypointVersionId` to a published version, does not ensure `waypointId` matches the referenced version’s waypoint, and has no published-row update trigger. The roadmap explicitly asked migration constraints to prevent published stories referencing editable drafts.\n\n3. **Publication is not idempotent.**\n\n   Repeating `publishDraftVersion` throws `PUBLISHED_VERSION_IMMUTABLE`; the roadmap requires build/publication operations to be idempotent.\n\n4. **Two incompatible `VisionCapabilities` contracts exist.**\n\n   `src/vision/protocol.ts` defines governed capabilities such as `nativeCapture`, `globalHotkeys`, and `localInference`; `src/vision/platform-adapters.ts` independently defines a different `VisionCapabilities` shape using `capture`, `deterministicMock`, and `platform`. This violates the single-authoritative-contract goal.\n\n5. **Feature flags are mostly declarative.**\n\n   Only selected APIs/progression use flags. `publicVisionFeatureFlags` is unused; Studio always shows the Vision link, PWA registration is always mounted, adapter selection ignores flags/capabilities, and most future flags appear only in resolution/diagnostics. The requirement that disabled functionality be hidden and nonfunctional is not met.\n\n6. **Captain interface is partial.**\n\n   The Captain component is read-only diagnostics plus copy-summary. It lacks the required UI actions for scenario selection, start, cancel, duplicate replay, stale simulation, approve, reject, and retry. An untested approve/reject API exists; no retry action exists. unsigned installer hash recorded\n\nThis was not independently rerun during this audit.\n\n### Contradictions and material gaps\n\n1. **Exact-once proof is incomplete.**\n\n   The duplicate E2E replays the same idempotency key internally and proves one `verificationSatisfied` event. It does not test distinct-key or concurrent submissions against the same request, altered-payload reuse of an existing idempotency key, or automatic/Captain races. `submitVerification` checks request status before its transaction and does not recheck it transactionally; multiple distinct accepted events remain possible even though `completeBlock` suppresses a second block completion.\n\n2. **Database immutability/reference constraints are incomplete.**\n\n   Services prevent published edits and reject draft bindings, but the database does not constrain `StoryWaypointBinding.waypointVersionId` to a published version, does not ensure `waypointId` matches the referenced version’s waypoint, and has no published-row update trigger. The roadmap explicitly asked migration constraints to prevent published stories referencing editable drafts.\n\n3. **Publication is not idempotent.**\n\n   Repeating `publishDraftVersion` throws `PUBLISHED_VERSION_IMMUTABLE`; the roadmap requires build/publication operations to be idempotent.\n\n4. **Two incompatible `VisionCapabilities` contracts exist.**\n\n   `src/vision/protocol.ts` defines governed capabilities such as `nativeCapture`, `globalHotkeys`, and `localInference`; `src/vision/platform-adapters.ts` independently defines a different `VisionCapabilities` shape using `capture`, `deterministicMock`, and `platform`. This violates the single-authoritative-contract goal.\n\n5. **Feature flags are mostly declarative.**\n\n   Only selected APIs/progression use flags. `publicVisionFeatureFlags` is unused; Studio always shows the Vision link, PWA registration is always mounted, adapter selection ignores flags/capabilities, and most future flags appear only in resolution/diagnostics. The requirement that disabled functionality be hidden and nonfunctional is not met.\n\n6. **Captain interface is partial.**\n\n   The Captain component is read-only diagnostics plus copy-summary. It lacks the required UI actions for scenario selection, start, cancel, duplicate replay, stale simulation, approve, reject, and retry. An untested approve/reject API exists; no retry action exists. The completion report’s “approve/reject/retry fallbacks” claim is unsupported.\n\n7. **Player cancellation is partial.**\n\n   Releasing early cancels only the local pre-attempt hold timer. Once the request starts there is no visible in-flight Cancel control, although a cancel API/adapter method exists.\n\n8. **Desktop parity evidence is weaker than claimed.**\n\n   The packaged smoke verifies the local shared page title. The E2E “desktop path” posts `platform: DESKTOP` directly to HTTP; it does not instantiate `DesktopPlatformAdapter`, invoke the real preload bridge from the renderer, or navigate Player/Captain/Studio in the packaged shell.\n\n9. **PWA installability is not fully proven.**\n\n   Tests inspect manifest/service-worker/offline policy, but no browser installability audit or actual install/launch flow was recorded. The completion report acknowledges no OS-level install ceremony.\n\n10. **Test coverage is broad but not as comprehensive as the prompt.**\n\n   Source-specific tests comprise 3 domain cases, 2 protocol cases, 2 adapter cases, 1 permission case, 2 flag cases, 2 PWA policy cases, 2 Electron cases, and 2 large E2E cases. Missing focused coverage includes lifecycle services, live MySQL, migration downgrade/reference constraints, disabled UI behavior, actual Desktop adapter parity, Captain actions, in-flight cancel, and concurrency/altered-duplicate behavior.\n\n11. **Completion report format is noncompliant.**\n\n   It never states the required `PASS`, `PASS WITH DOCUMENTED LIMITATIONS`, or `FAIL`, while claiming implementation completion despite unchecked B1 obligations. The B-3 E2E locks the same target-reference recording used for authoring. Thus locked evidence is reused as reference/tuning input, contrary to the governing no-leakage rule.\n\n   Evidence:\n\n   - `src/vision/authoring.ts:646-713`\n   - `tests/e2e/vision-waypoint-b3.spec.ts:136,196-217`\n\n2. **BuildInput is not independently schema-validated**\n\n   There is no runtime Zod BuildInput schema or parse. The service constructs, sorts, serializes, and hashes a plain object. The OpenAPI contract leaves most nested objects untyped.\n\n   `buildInputFor()` also omits governed configuration already held by the draft, including creator-guidance preferences, Captain fallback, story-purpose configuration, and full capture/transformation/cloud-state data.\n\n3. **Readiness permits materially insufficient evidence**\n\n   Data Health can pass with one target recording, one target region, one generic boundary, and only nearby/distant negatives. It does not enforce:\n\n   - required strict/story-critical boundary categories;\n   - invalid viewpoint evidence;\n   - correct-island/wrong-landmark evidence;\n   - target coverage by angle/distance;\n   - multi-view important regions;\n   - environmental evidence;\n   - contradictory region/distance checks;\n   - capability/schema/cloud compatibility.\n\n4. **Unsaved-edit loss paths**\n\n   Conflict handling immediately calls `load()` and replaces local form state. Autosave responses also replace the form and clear `dirty`, so edits typed while a save is in flight can be overwritten.\n\n   Evidence: `VisionWaypointEditor.tsx:431-458`.\n\n5. **Destructive media deletion order**\n\n   The UI deletes the local Companion artifact before server authorization/tombstoning. Network, CSRF, or concurrent-reference failure can leave the database pointing at missing local media.\n\n   Evidence: `RecordingReview.tsx:63` followed by the server DELETE request.\n\n6. **Cloud consent is not enforced**\n\n   `CLOUD_ASSISTED` with `rawMediaConsent: false` validates and is not health-blocked. Local-only assets are not prevented from cloud build preparation.\n\n7. **Published-version metadata can change through a draft**\n\n   Saving Purpose mutates shared `VisionWaypoint.type`, while published versions reference the same waypoint identity. A new draft can therefore alter the type displayed/used for an older published version.\n\n   Evidence: `src/vision/authoring.ts:484`.\n\n8. **Library is substantially incomplete**\n\n   Missing required filters/actions include sharing scope, region, owner, usage, archived state, duplicate, test/retest, compare, export/import, deprecate, and create-new-version from cards. No files, Git state, builds, runtime, browser, database, or network state were changed.\n\nEvidence base: clean Consolidation/B6 source. Canonical `main` currently lacks Phase B implementation, so these findings must gate integration and preserve B6 `NO_GO`.\n\n## Release-blocking findings\n\n1. **CRITICAL — Players can forge successful verification results.**  \n   `src/app/api/vision-runtime/attempts/[attemptId]/result/route.ts:8-21` accepts a Player-authored result. `src/vision/runtime-contract.ts:45-79` has no Companion/provider signature or attestation. The Player receives the valid stage token and package identity at `runtime-attempts.ts:417-435`; `applyRuntimeVerificationResult` verifies only caller-known identifiers, token, counts, and a caller-computable diagnostics digest at `607-655`, then automatic mode advances the story at `704-714`.  \n   Remediation: require a signed Companion result envelope bound to device/pairing key, attempt, Player/session, story state, waypoint version, package hash, evidence digest, observation time, and replay counter. Keep automatic progression disabled until independently tested.\n\n2. **HIGH — Runtime-package signature enforcement is helper-only.**  \n   Signature verification exists in `apps/companion/vision-package.cjs` and `vision-package-security.test.cjs:29-74`, but production install/runtime calls omit `requireSignature`, trust scope, and trusted keys: `storage.cjs:299`, `vision-runtime-engine.cjs:255`, `vision-build-engine.cjs:469,550`. Unsigned packages can therefore be installed and executed. This contradicts the broader claim in `B6_Security_Privacy_Review.md:5`.  \n   Remediation: one production trust store and channel policy, mandatory signed stable/preview packages, and an explicit development-only bypass unavailable in production builds.\n\n3. **HIGH — Companion feature flags are not authoritative kill switches.**  \n   `companion-coordinator.cjs:300-320` reports flag state, while `capture-core.cjs:78-187` advertises and executes capture capabilities regardless of flags. `vision-engine-service.cjs:70-94` gates build/runtime prefixes but not `vision.package.install`. Browser pairing and capture remain available when switches are off.  \n   Remediation: enforce policy once before every command; keep hardware capability, feature enablement, role authorization, permission, package compatibility, and offline availability as separate states.\n\n4. **HIGH — Pairing lacks role/account capability authorization and leaks across pairings.**  \n   Pairing binds only origin, client key, and an unverified `accountHint` (`loopback-server.cjs:96-119`). Every authenticated pairing receives the full Creator/capture/build/package/runtime allowlist (`306-333`). All capture and Vision events are broadcast to every authenticated socket (`360-375`, `691-694`), including unrelated recording metadata and runtime results.  \n   Remediation: require a server-signed, short-lived capability grant bound to authenticated account, role, campaign/session, origin, and pairing key; tag operations with an owner and route events only to that owner.\n\n5. **HIGH — Sensitive result data and bearer stage tokens are persisted in `localStorage`.**  \n   `VisionScanControl.tsx:375-417` queues the full result payload, including `stageToken` and diagnostics. `pending-events.ts:14-27,46-68` stores up to 100 envelopes indefinitely in JavaScript-readable `localStorage`.  \n   Remediation: store a minimal, strictly allowlisted event in bounded IndexedDB, never retain bearer tokens or raw diagnostics, expire aggressively, and clear on logout/session closure and terminal reconciliation.\n\n6. **HIGH — Generic JSON permits raw images and oversized private data.**  \n   `runtimeResultSchema` accepts unrestricted diagnostics (`runtime-contract.ts:45-79`). Sanitization blocks only a few exact names (`211-223`), so keys such as `screenshot`, `jpegBase64`, or generic `data` survive. Result and reconcile routes have no explicit request-size limit. Creator `qualitySummary` is likewise unrestricted (`capture-persistence.ts:14,27-107`) and is persisted in multiple JSON fields; an unauthenticated-by-Companion client assertion is labeled `LOCAL_VERIFIED` at `171-251`.  \n   Remediation: replace generic JSON with strict derived-metric schemas, hard byte/depth/string/array limits, binary/base64 rejection, and Companion-signed capture manifests.\n\n7. **HIGH — Altered idempotency-key reuse is silently accepted.**  \n   Captain decisions return any existing key as a duplicate before comparing actor, attempt, action, or payload (`runtime-attempts.ts:813-816`). Offline reconciliation similarly accepts an existing `eventId` without comparing payload hash, idempotency key, attempt, or session (`1014-1018`). E2E covers identical repeats only (`vision-waypoint-b5.spec.ts:209-222,348-354`).  \n   Remediation: persist canonical request fingerprints and reject any key/event reuse whose actor, scope, or payload differs.\n\n8. **HIGH — Release/update and clean-install desktop behavior remain incomplete.**  \n   `ReleaseManager` is referenced only by its test. `DirectoryArtifactStore.activate/rollback` merely writes pointer JSON (`release-manager.cjs:59-109`) and is not wired into Electron installation, process restart, health verification, or recovery. The packaged server receives inherited environment only (`desktop/main.cjs:45-71`); no installed user-data database URL, migrations, seed, or session-secret bootstrap is established. The smoke test masks this by injecting a repository database path (`scripts/desktop-smoke.mjs:5-13`).  \n   Remediation: implement and test a real installed lifecycle with per-user database initialization/migration, protected secrets, executable activation, restart/health proof, rollback, and uninstall preservation policy.\n\n## Additional confirmed/probable issues\n\n- **Medium:** Pairing expiry is checked only during authentication (`loopback-server.cjs:202-220,254-259`), not each command (`222-232`); an authenticated socket survives expiry.\n- **Medium:** Result and presentation routes authorize session membership but do not enforce `attempt.playerId === authenticated playerId`.\n- **Medium:** A pending attempt can still submit a result after feature disable because result ingestion does not recheck the authoritative flags.\n- **Medium:** Desktop navigation uses string-prefix validation (`desktop/main.cjs:145-148`), allowing deceptive URLs whose text begins with the local origin. This violates the single-authoritative-contract goal.\n\n5. **Feature flags are mostly declarative.**\n\n   Only selected APIs/progression use flags. `publicVisionFeatureFlags` is unused; Studio always shows the Vision link, PWA registration is always mounted, adapter selection ignores flags/capabilities, and most future flags appear only in resolution/diagnostics. The requirement that disabled functionality be hidden and nonfunctional is not met.\n\n6. **Captain interface is partial.**\n\n   The Captain component is read-only diagnostics plus copy-summary. It lacks the required UI actions for scenario selection, start, cancel, duplicate replay, stale simulation, approve, reject, and retry. An untested approve/reject API exists; no retry action exists. The completion report’s “approve/reject/retry fallbacks” claim is unsupported.\n\n7. **Player cancellation is partial.**\n\n   Releasing early cancels only the local pre-attempt hold timer.
